It is, therefore, expected from the society that this judicial power exercised by the court should not be interfered with by the executive government in exercise of its power of remission under section 401 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">84.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Similarly the court of sessions within the meaning of section 6(1) of the Code of Criminal Procedure authorises to award a sentence of death or imprisonment for life in respect of an offence punishable under section 120B read with section 302 of the Penal Code. There are other corresponding provisions in the special laws empowering different tribunals to award capital sentence and imprisonment for life. The High Court Division has exercised the power under the general as well as substantive law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">85.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This court while commuting the sentence of death in criminal appeal Nos.39-40 of 2013 directed that the accused shall suffer imprisonment till the rest of life. In the latter case, this court while commuting the sentence observed that the sentence of imprisonment for rest of life would be ‘proportionate to the gravity of the crimes’ committed by him. Though this court did not mention sections 45 and 53, it made the above direction keeping those provisions in consideration. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">86.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 35A of the Code of Criminal Procedure is not applicable in case of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life. An accused person cannot claim the deduction of the period in custody prior to the conviction as of right. It is a discretionary power of the court. It cannot be applicable in respect of an offence which is punishable with death. Though the word ‘only’ is used in section 35A, the legislature without considering section 401 of the Code of Criminal Procedure and section 53 of the Penal Code has inserted the word ‘only’ but the use of word ‘only’ will not make any difference since under the scheme of the prevailing laws any remission/reduction of sentence has been reserved to the government only. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">87.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">More so, as observed above, if the sentence of imprisonment for life is treated as imprisonment for the whole of the remaining period of the convicted person’s natural life, how the court will deduct from the sentence of imprisonment, the total period the accused has suffered in custody before trial. This section 35A is  almost similar to section 428 of the Indian Code of Criminal Procedure. The Supreme Court held that the benefit of set-off under section 428 is not available to life convicts. (Katar Singh V. State of Haryana, AIR 1982 S.C. 1439). We would like to observe here that the draftsmen or the Legislature without understanding the correct meaning and/or the tenor of sections 45, 53 and 57 of the Penal Code substituted the words ‘rigorous imprisonment for thirty years’ for the words ‘rigorous imprisonment for twenty years’ in section 57 by Ordinance No.XLI of 1985 presuming that the period of life sentence was twenty years, and increased it to ‘thirty years’. The Legislature should keep in mind that the Law Commission of British India took 36 years in finalising the Penal Code. It should not amend any provision without consultation with the experts dealing with the subject lest ends of justice is not defeated. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">88.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">From the above discussions this court hold that the court while exercising the power in awarding punishment prescribed in the Penal Code under legal obligation see that the imposition of punishment is commensurate to the nature of the crime committed by the offender and in that process no injustice is caused either to the victim or to the accused who has committed the crime. This exercise of power by the court is a judicial power. However, the executive power to be exercised by the President under article 49 pardoning an offender even after confirmation of death sentence or confirmation of life imprisonment can be exercised in appropriate case. This judicial power cannot be curtailed and/or interfered with by an action of the executive by exercising executive power either under the provisions of the Jail Code or under section 401 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. If on consideration of the nature of offence committed by the offender and taking consideration of the interest of the victim and the accused, commutes the sentence of death till life by this court or the High Court Division with findings that such imposition of punishment is commensurate to the nature of the crime committed and in that process no injustice is caused to the victim and that the sentence of twenty or thirty years would be grossly inadequate and disproportionate, this category of cases would be beyond application of remission, because while imposing a modified punishment providing for any specific term of incarceration or till the end of convicts life as the alternative to death sentence can only be exercised by the High Court Division and this court and not by any other inferior tribunal or the executive. Accordingly, we conclude our opinion as under:-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">1)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">A sentence of death awarded to an offender under section 302 of the Penal Code is the rule and life imprisonment is an exception. The court may commute death sentence to life imprisonment of a prisoner on extenuating circumstances and in that case it must assign reasons therefore.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">2)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Life imprisonment within the meaning of section 53 read with section 45 of the Penal Code means imprisonment for rest of the life of the convict.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">3)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">If the High Court Division or this court commutes a sentence of death to imprisonment for life and direct that the prisoner shall have to suffer rest of his natural life, such type of cases would be beyond the application of remission.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 57 of the Penal Code is only for the purpose of working out the fractions of the maximum sentence fixed for the principal offence, that is to say, if such provision is not made, it would have been impossible to work out the fractions of an indefinite term. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Remission contained in Chapter XXI of the Bengal Jail Code, volume 1(Part I) are administrative instructions regarding various remissions. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">If an offender pleads guilty at the initial stage of the trial of the case in respect of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life, the court/tribunal shall take lenient view on the question of awarding sentence, but in such cases, the court shall ascertain as to whether the offender pleading guilty upon understanding the offence charged with against him before accepting such plea. Provided however that the court is not bound to accept all pleas of guilty and award the minimum sentence. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In exercise of power under article 49 of the constitution the President has power to grant pardon, reprieves and respite and to remit, suspend or commute any sentence even after the commutation of sentence by this court or the High Court Division.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: list 24.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">89.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The appeal, is therefore, dismissed with commutation of the sentence of the appellants to imprisonment for rest of the life. Let a copy of this judgment be communicated to the Secretary, Ministry of Home Affairs and the Inspector General of Prisons for information and taking steps in respect of life sentence prisoners.       </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10pt; font-variant: small-caps; color: black;">Criminal Appeal Nos. 15-16 of 2010. </span></u></strong></a><u></u></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span style="font-size: 9pt; color: black;">(From the judgment and order dated 29.10.2007 &amp; 30.10.2007</span><span style="font-size: 9pt;"> passed by the High Court Division in Death Reference No.127 of 2003 with Criminal Appeal No.3895 of 2003 and Jail Appeal No.739 of 2003<span style="color: black;">.)</span></span></span></p></div></div></div></div>

Name="Medium List 1 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="66" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 2 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="67" <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 4"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="64" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 2 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="65" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium List 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">}</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -3.7pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Capt. S.M. Nasirul Huq and others</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt -.05in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . Petitioners</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt -.05in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">VERSUS</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -3.7pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate, represent by it Manager, 141-143, Motijheel Commercial Area, Police Station- Motijheel, Dhaka- 1000 and others </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -3.7pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . Respondents.</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Article 102</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">State Acquisition Rules, 1955</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Rules 27, 30, 31 and 42A</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 107%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">This Court finds that the sequence of work under Rule 27 is to be adhered to strictly and a clear reading of Rule 42A reveals that a corrective exercise thereunder can only be embarked upon at a stage intermediate between stages <em>(ix)</em> and <em>(x) </em>enumerated under Rule 27.</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">In the facts as submitted by the Petitioners it is noted that the impugned intervention under Rule 42A came post-preparation and publication of the Record-of-Right as in stage <em>(x)</em> under Rule 27 above in a manner not contemplated under the Rules. As aptly submitted by Mr. Golam Arshed for the Petitioner the only avenue at that juncture available to the Respondents, if at all, for a correction of the relevant S.A. Record-of-Rights was to agitate their case before a civil court. That is indeed a view, this Court finds, that has clearly been </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">enunciated earlier by this Court and affirmed </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">by the Appellate Division in a series of Writ Petitions already identified hereinbefore and </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">generated incidentally under the related appeals</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">of the Respondent No.1 under Rule 42A. Rules</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;"> Nisi issued in all those Writ Petitions were </span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">notably made absolute by this Court’s common</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;"> Judgment and Order dated 20.5.2008.</span></strong> <strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">By reason of the above and the findings of its own as above stated, this Court finds merit in the Application and substance in the Rule issued.        . . . (6, 8 and 11)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Romisa Khanam Vs. Bangladesh in 61 DLR (2009), 18 and Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate Vs. Rasheda Begum and others, 14 MLR (AD) 2009, 401 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Golam Arshed, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the Petitioners.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">. . . For the Respondent No. 1 </span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Amit Talukder, DAG</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">… For the Respondents. </span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;">JUDGMENT</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 30.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">Syed Refaat Ahmed, J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">In this Application</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> under Article 102 of the Constitution a Rule Nisi was issued calling upon the Respondents to show cause as to why the impugned Judgment and Order dated 10.2.2003 passed on rehearing by the Respondent No. 7 Appeal Officer-in-Charge and Assistant Settlement Officer and approved by the Respondent No. 6 Settlement Officer, Dhaka on 6.3.2003 in Appeal Case Nos. 2480 and 2481 of 1999 (as similarly done in Appeal Nos. 2463-2467, 2471-2474, 2476, 2478-2479, 2482-2488, 2490-2501 of 1999) under Rule 31 of The Tenancy Rules, 1955 (“Rules”) setting aside the earlier decision dated 22.11.99 passed by the same Office in the same Appeals should not be declared to have been passed without any lawful authority and is of no legal effect and not binding upon the Petitioners or such other or further Order or Orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">The Petitioner’s case in short is that the 3.49 acres of land of C.S Plot No. 139, Khatian No. 2 of Mouza Rajabazaar, Dhaka inclusive of the Petitioner’s 0.63 acre land originally belonged to the Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate, Respondent No. 1 who settled the said land in 1927 and after wholesale acquisition of such lands under the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950 (“Act”) the disputed land vested upon the Government. The Petitioners <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">assert that consequently they became Government</span> tenants and had their names recorded in S.A. Record. It is also asserted that under the Metro or Mahanagar Survey that more recently took place, the Petitioners’ said 0.63 acre of land of C.S. Plot No. 139 has been recorded in their name at the <em>“Tasdik”</em> or recording stage. But all on a sudden the Respondent No. 1 filed Objection Case Nos. 230 and 231 for recording its name in Metro Khatian No. 2563 Plot No. 2635, 2638 and 2639 and Khatian No. 2526 only on the ground that the C.S. Khatian No. 2 stands in their name. That claim of the Respondent No.1 was rejected upon hearing all parties concerned by the Judgments and Orders dated 25.11.1999 and 29.12.1999. Against said Judgments and Orders the Respondent No. 1 preferred Appeal Nos. 2480 and 2481 of 1999 under Rule 31 of the Rules which were also rejected analogously along with other similar appeals by the Respondent No. 7 Settlement <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">Officer’s Judgment and Order dated 22.11.1999.</span> Three years later, the Respondent No. 1 Manager of Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate filed an Application on 14.7.2002 to the Settlement Officer, Dhaka to rehear the previously disallowed Rule 31 Appeal Case Nos. 2463 to 2501 of 1999 (inclusive of Appeal Nos. 2480 and 2481 of 1999) by invoking in that regard Rule 42A of the Rules. On the basis of the said application, the Respondent No.7 Officer reheard all the Appeals and allowed the same by his Judgment and Order dated 10.2.2003 as approved by the Respondent No. 6 Settlement Officer, Dhaka on 6.3.2003. Against the said impugned Order dated 10.2.2003 passed in Appeal Nos. 2480 and 2481 of 1999 the present Petitioners have filed the instant Writ Petition and obtained the Rule. On the other hand, Romisa Khatun and others also filed Writ Petition Nos. 2678 of 2005, 3797 of 2003, 6671 of 2004, 6262 of 2005 and 1512-13 of 2006 against the said Judgment and Order dated 10.2.2003 stemming from the other appeals. It is in this context that the Petitioners challenge the impugned Order to record the disputed land in the name of Respondent No. 1 as being illegal and without any lawful authority.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">The Petitioners assert that the disputed lands in C.S Plot No. 139 were not in the list of choice land of the Respondent No. 1 and as such the Respondent No.1 lost all rent-receiving interest in such land on and from April 1956 under a Gazetted Notification of 1956 published under the Act and as such the Respondent No.1 has illegally claimed ownership of the disputed land. Consequently, the impugned second appellate Judgment and Order dated 10.2.2003 recognizing such claim of the Respondent No.1 is submitted to be illegal and beyond the provisions of law.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Drawing on the terms of the Bhawal Raj Court Manager’s application of 14.72002 the Petitioners’ learned Advocate Mr. Golam Arshed has argued at the outset that the Rule 31 Appeal Nos. 2480 and 2481 of 1999 being once disallowed by Respondent No. 7, such Appeal Officer is not entitled to reopen and rehear the same under the same provision of law or rule. Instead, it was for the concerned Respondent Nos. 6 and 7 to recognize at this juncture that the initial rejection Orders disfavouring the Respondent No. 1 aptly reflect the scheme of the law and the Rules in particular. That is, the Petitioners having had their names duly recorded in the S.A. Record-of-Rights, the details of such finally prepared and published Record were also reflected in the draft Mahanagar or the Metro Survey. In such a case, the only option available to the Respondent No. 1 was to challenge the S.A. Record through a civil suit brought before an appropriate forum. There, in the facts, remained neither any residual right vested in the Respondent No. 1 Bhawal Raj Court nor any authority in the Respondent Nos. 6 and 7 Settlement Officers under the Rules to instead delve into the facts and circumstances of the publication of the final S.A. Record in the Petitioners’ favour. Moreover, it is submitted on behalf of the Petitioners that Rule 42A of the Rules exceptionally provides for a correction of entry provided there is established a ground of fraudulent entry and that such correction is sought prior to final publication of Record-of-Rights. Neither of these ingredients, Mr. Golam Arshed submits, are present in the Respondent No. 1’s case. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">This Court has, in consideration of the submissions above, perused in particular the provisions on <em>Appeal</em> and <em>Preparation of Final</em> <em>Records</em> in Rules 31 and 32 respectively of the Rules and finds no sanction therein for:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level6 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 3.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(a)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">rehearing a final order of initial appeal; and </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level6 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">(b)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">objections to be entertained after preparation and publication of final record. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Indeed, Rule 31 only permits of a single appellate process resulting in a final order on any such appeal.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Petitioners’ case is also significantly focused on the justifiability of interference under Rule 42A of Rules at the stage of revision of Record-of-Rights under Section 144 of the Act. Rule 27 of Chapter VII of the Rules enumerates sequentially the stages of the work involved in this regard and reads thus:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“27. Stages of the work:­­- The work shall ordinarily consist of the following stages, namely: </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(i)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">     </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">traverse survey;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(ii)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">   </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">cadastral survey; </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 1.0in 1.5in 2.0in 2.5in 3.0in 251.4pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(iii) </span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">erection of boundary marks;   </span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(iv)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">  </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">preliminary record-writing (Khanapuri);</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(v)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">local explanation (Bujharat);</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 1.0in 1.5in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(vi)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">  </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">attestation;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 84.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(vii)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">publication of draft record;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 84.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(viii)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">disposal of objections;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 1.0in 1.5in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(ix)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">  </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">filing of appeals and disposal thereof;</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 1.0in 1.5in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(x)<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">    </span></span></em><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">preparation and publication of final record.”</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt 1.0in 1.5in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">This Court finds that the sequence of work under Rule 27 is to be adhered to strictly and a clear reading of Rule 42A reveals that a corrective exercise thereunder can only be embarked upon at a stage intermediate between stages <em>(ix)</em> and <em>(x) </em>enumerated under Rule 27. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt 1.0in 1.5in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Rule 42A finds its place under Chapter VIII of the Rules, with this Chapter being devoted to the powers of Revenue Officers in revising Record-of-Rights under Section 144. Rule 42A reads thus:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 24.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“42A. <strong>Correction of fraudulent entry before final publication of record-of-rights-</strong> The Revenue-officer, with the additional designation of “Settlement Officer” shall, on receipt of an application or on receipt of an official report for the correction of an entry <u>that has been procured by fraud in record-of-rights before final publication thereof</u>, after consulting relevant records and making such other enquires as he deems necessary, direct excision of the fraudulent entry and his act in doing so shall not be open to appeal. At the same time, the Revenue-officer shall make the correct entry after giving the parties concerned a hearing and recording his finding in a formal proceeding for the purpose of future reference.” </span></em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(Emphasis added by this Court)</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the facts as submitted by the Petitioners it is noted that the impugned intervention under Rule 42A came post-preparation and publication of the Record-of-Right as in stage <em>(x)</em> under Rule 27 above in a manner not contemplated under the Rules. As aptly submitted by Mr. Golam Arshed for the Petitioner the only avenue at that juncture available to the Respondents, if at all, for a correction of the relevant S.A. Record-of-Rights was to agitate their case before a civil court. That is indeed a view, this Court finds, that has clearly been enunciated earlier by this Court and affirmed by the Appellate Division in a series of Writ Petitions already identified hereinbefore and generated incidentally under the related appeals of the Respondent No.1 under Rule 42A. Rules Nisi issued in all those Writ Petitions were notably made absolute by this Court’s common Judgment and Order dated 20.5.2008.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">          </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The impugned second appellate Judgments and Orders in all those Writ Petitions order were declared to have been passed without any lawful authority and to be of no legal effect and the first appellate Orders dismissing the appeals of the Respondent Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate presented under Rule 31 of the Rules were, consequentially, restored by this Court. That Judgment reported as <em>Romisa Khanam</em> vs. <em>Bangladesh</em> in <em>61 DLR(2009), 18</em> gave rise to Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal Nos. 1447-1452 of 2008 before the Appellate Division. The Appellate Division’s Judgment and Order dated 14.7.2009 dismissing all the said Civil Petitions by the Judgment and Order dated 14.7.2009 is found reported as <em>Bhawal Raj Court of Wards Estate vs. Rasheda Begum &amp; ors. </em>in<em> 14 MLR (AD) 2009, 401.</em> The ratio decidendi of the Appellate Division’s Judgment to which this Court wholly subscribes to for reasons as explained hereinabove and as applies to the similar facts in this instant Writ Petition is quoted herein below:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">“The Learned Advocate appearing for the leave petitioner, when confronted with the aforesaid gazette notifications dated 24.03.1952 and 29.02.1952, as to acquisition of rent receiving interest and the vesting of lands of the leave petitioners, including the case lands, found it difficult to substantiate the locus standi of leave petitioner in challenging the draft records of right prepared in the names of the respective writ petitioners in respect of their respective case lands prepared during the Mohanagar Survey. Further with the publication of the gazette notifications dated 24.3.1952 and 29.2.1956 the leave petitioner ceased to have any right, title and interest and possession in the case lands, because of acquisition, and vesting of rent receiving interest of said lands in the Government.</span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On plain reading of the Rule 42A, quoted above, it appears that the settlement officer is empowered to pass order only on receipt of an application or on receipt of an official report, for correction of an entry in the record of right, procured by fraud, before final publication thereof. <u>Thus the said Rule cannot be applicable in the instant case inasmuch as the record of right as prepared is in accordance with the past records of right prepared during S.A. Operation and R.S.  Operation and there being no change as to the names as appearing in the said records of right the question of fraud in recording the entry of names in the recent record of right prepared after the Mohanagar Survey  does not arise. Apart from that after final publication of the record of right, after the S.A. Survey the only mode for correction of the same was through civil court and thus subsequent to preparation of S.A. record of right, the R.S. record of right was prepared and after final publication thereof the mode for correction of any wrong entry appearing in the R.S record was through Civil Court and without moving the Civil Court no correction in those records of right is lawful or permissible and as such the draft record of right in the instant case having been prepared following the preparation of the S.A. and R.S. records in accordance with law, the attempts of the leave petitioner for  correction under Rules-30 and 31 of the State Acquisition Rules, 1955 have failed. The plain reading of the application dated 14.7.2002,</u> quoted above, <u>allegedly filed under Rule 42A of the State Acquisition Rules, 1955, said application do not contain any specific allegation of any act of fraud and it is the settled principle of law that an application, not having disclosed any act of fraud in its body, is not entertainable and liable to be rejected. Without correcting the S.A Khatian and R.S. Khatian as prepared <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">in respect of the case lands in accordance</span> with law earlier, the leave petitioner cannot get its name entered in the recent record of right prepared during Mahanagar Survey allegedly only on the basis of C.S. Khatian.</u></span></em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Thus we are of the view that the leave petitioner had not locus-<span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">standi to challenge the draft Mahanagar</span> <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">Survey Khatian as prepared in the names</span> of the respective writ petitioners, at-least after publication of the gazette notifications dated 24.3.1952 and 29.2.1952”</span></em><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">(Emphasis added by this Court)<em>.</em></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the respondents Mr. Md. Nurul Amin has candidly acknowl-edged the applicability the binding effect of the said Appellate Division Judgment to the facts and circumstances arising under the instant Writ Petition and finds, resultantly no ground to oppose this Rule.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">By reason of the above and the findings of its own as above stated, this Court finds merit in the Application and substance in the Rule issued. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute. </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">13.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">      </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">There is no Order as to costs. </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent3" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 24.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">        Communicate this Order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><em><u><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></em></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">Writ Pet</span></strong></a><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">ition No. 3979 of 2003</span></strong></span></p></div></div></div></div>
532	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Dabendra Kumar Guha Vs. Most. Nur Begum 2017 (2) LNJ 86</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> First Appeal No. 54 of 2011 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker. J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Md. Aminul Islam, Mr. Ashim Kumar Mallik,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2017 (2) LNJ 86</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Dabendra Kumar Guha </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Most. Nur Begum </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Civil Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2017-09-18</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <w:WordDocument>  <w:View>Normal</w:View>  <w:Zoom>0</w:Zoom>
