roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">}</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 105%; margin: 0in -1.45pt 3.0pt -1.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">Khan Mohammad Ameer and another </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 105%; margin: 0in -1.45pt 3.0pt -1.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 105%; letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">.. Appellants </span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 105%; margin: 0in -1.45pt 3.0pt -1.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 105%;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -.7pt; tab-stops: 15.95pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Atiqur Rahman and others </span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: -7.0pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11pt;">... Respondents</span></em></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Contract Act (IX of 1872)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Sections 202 and 203</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case from the deed of revocation of power of attorney, it appears that the principal revoked it assigning the reasons amongst others to the effect that- “as the purpose for which the attorney was appointed has been exhausted and in the context of the present unavailable circumstances, we have decided to handle the mater directly and by ourselves.” Except the power of attorney executed couple with interest all other power may be revoked at any time by the principal.  From the recital of the power of attorney, it does not appear that the agent herself has an interest in the property and hence such agency can be revoked unilaterally without prejudice of such interest.                                             . . .(10)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Contract Act (IX of 1872)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Sections 202 and 203</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It appears that the provision for giving notice before cancellation of power of attorney has been incorporated in the new enactment of the Powers of Attorney Act of 2012 which was not expressly provided in repealed Act of 1982 thereof. It is not imperative to settle that the notice was served or not before cancellation of the power as we are of the opinion that the power of attorney in question is not a power coupled with interest and hence the same is revocable. Furthermore, since the power of attorney was revoked on 27.09.2009 before coming into force of new enactment of 2012, as such, giving notice or no notice  has not debarred the principal to revoke it as the same appears do not have coupled with interest of the agent.       . . . (10)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">67 DLR (AD) 240; AIR 1969 (SC) 73; 16 BLD 519 and BLT (AD) 1 ref.</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Qumrul Haque Siddique and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Abdul Barek Chowdhury, Advocates </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the appellants</span></em></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. A.J. Mohammad Ali with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">…For the respondents</span></em></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;">JUDGMENT</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mohammad Ullah, J</span></u></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">:</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> This First Appeal has been sent from the office of the Honourable Chief Justice for disposal by this Division Bench by order dated 12.02.2017. The above numbered First Appeal has been preferred by the plaintiff against the judgment and decree dated 20.11.2014 passed by the learned Joint</span> <span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 94 of 2011 dismissing the suit. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts leading to the disposal of the appeal is as follows: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         The appellant as plaintiff instituted Title Suit No. 94 of 2011 in the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka against the defendants-respondents with a prayer that the power of attorney No. 11363 dated 04.08.1999 is still in force and the deed of cancellation of power of attorney No. 8427 dated 29.07.2010 is illegal, void, unauthorized and without jurisdiction. The case of the plaintiff-appellant is that the suit land originally belonged to one Matiur Rahman who got the same as perpetual lease on 13.03.1961 for 99 years from the then Dhaka Improvement Trust (DIT) now RAJUK. Motiur Rahman while in possession transferred the same in favour of his full brother Habibur Rahman on 31.03.1969 by a registered deed. Habibur Rahman while in peaceful possession died leaving four daughters, namely, Nabila Rahman, Nazia Rahman, Saddat Rahman and Sadia Rahman, only son Md. Atiqur Rahman and wife Meherunnessa to inherit him. While aforesaid heirs of Habibur Rahman having been in peaceful possession they mutated their names in the office of RAJUK on 19.01.1989. The heirs of Habibur Rahman entered into an unregistered deed of agreement for sale of the property with the plaintiff No.1 on 07.07.1987 fixing the price for an amount of Taka 70,00,000/- on receiving  a sum of Taka 15,00,000/-. Thereafter the defendants No. 1-5 and their mother Meherunnessa received a total sum of Taka 39,50,000/- from the plaintiff No. 1 on different dates by cash, pay order and cheques. The said amount of money has been taken by the defendants by signing on the reverse side of the bainapatra. The defendants in that way took an amount of Taka 54,50,000/- out of total fixed price of Taka 70 lac. The mother of the defendants Meherunnessa died leaving them as legal heirs and successors. The defendants No. 1-5 executed and registered second deed of agreement for sale No. 11363 dated 04.08.1999 with the plaintiff No.1 acknowledging the receipt of Taka 54,50,000/- and at the time of execution of the second bainapatra, the defendants took an amount of Taka 1 lac only. Thereby in total they received Taka 55,50,000/- fixing  the date for performance of second bainapatra within five years and the parties also further agreed that the period of performance  of second bainapatra to be extended with the consent of both the parties. On the same day that is on 04.08.1999, the defendants No. 1-5 also executed and registered power of attorney No. 11634 nominating the plaintiff No. 2, the wife of plaintiff No. 1 Roksona Ameer giving certain powers in order to manage and control the property including the sale thereof. The defendants No. 1-5 also received an amount of Taka 19,42,500/- on different dates from 04.08.1999 to 10.03.2007 from the plaintiff No. 1 by signing at the reverse page of bainapatra as well as in some vouchers of the company of the plaintiff No. 1. One Niamat Ali Sheikh being the tenant of defendants No. 1-5 filed Title Suit No. 210 of 1986 for specific performance of contract in the 1<sup>st</sup>  Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka which was subsequently transferred  in the Court of Arth Rin Adalat and Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka and renumbered as Title Suit No. 1 of 2000(G) in which  RAJUK was a party and the plaintiff of the aforesaid suit obtained an order of injunction on 08.01.2001 restraining the defendants No. 2-6 from transferring the property to anybody else. While the defendants No. 1-5 and their mother Meherunnessa filed Title Suit No. 61 of 1989 in the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of Joint District Judge, Dhaka which was transferred in the Court of Artha Rin Adalat and Joint District Judge, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Dhaka and renumbered as Title Suit No. 2 of 2000 (G) for eviction of said Niamat Ali who was the tenant of the former. The plaintiff No. 1 of the instant suit Khan Md. Ameer was made a party to the suit for specific performance of contract filed by Niamat Ali Sheikh as defendant No. 10 on 30.11.1999. The power of attorney holder Roksona Ameer that is the wife of Khan Md. Ameer was also made a party to that suit as defendant No. 11 on 02.10.2001. The defendant No. 1 Atiqur Rahman himself filed an application for adding Roksona Ameer in the suit. After being added in the suit against Niamat Ali Sheikh,   Roksona Ameer filed vokalatnama, engaged lawyer for conducting the suit and spent money from time to time. Both the suits that is Title Suit No. 1 of 2000 (G) and Title Suit No. 2 of 2000(G) were heard analogously and the Title Suit No. 1 of 2000(G) was dismissed and the Title Suit No. 2 of 2000(G) was decreed. Against which Niamat Ali Sheikh filed First Appeal No. 194 of 2003 and First Appeal No. 303 of 2003 before this Court in which the plaintiff No. 1 was the defendant No. 9 and the plaintiff No. 2 was the defendant No. 10 and the RAJUK was the defendant No. 7. Both the said appeals were heard analogously and remitted to the trial Court on remand. The plaintiff No. 2 on the basis of power of attorney filed C.P. No. 406 of 2008 and C. P. No. 404 of 2008 and the Appellate Division granted leave on 11.03.2009 and the plaintiff No. 2 filed Civil Appeal No. 201 of 2009 and Civil Appeal No. 202 of 2009. In both the suits RAJUK was a party and there was an order of injunction against the RAJUK refraining it from giving sale permission in favour of the plaintiff No.2. The plaintiff No. 2 on the request of defendants No. 1-5  rescheduled, the price of the land for an amount of Taka 2,20,00,000/- and the defendants took an amount of Taka 30,00,000/-  executing  another agreement for sale on 04.10.2009 that is called third bainapatra. Thereafter on 19.11.2009, the plaintiff No. 2 as attorney of the defendants No. 1-5 executed another agreement for sale with the plaintiff No. 1 fixing the earlier sale price of Taka 2,20,00,000/-. The plaintiff No. 2 took an amount of Taka 1,19,80,000/- on 19.11.2009 from the plaintiff No. 1 by executing and registering  the deed of agreement for sale No. 10237 dated 19.11.2009. In this way, the defendants No. 1-5, their mother, and their attorney took an amount of total Taka 2,19,80,000/- from the plaintiff  No. 1. The plaintiffs deposited the rest amount of Taka 20,000/- in order to get a decree for specific performance of contract. The defendants No. 1-5 during pendency of the suit, tried to transfer of the property elsewhere in collusion with each other and as such the plaintiffs published a warning notice in the daily Ittefaq on 27.07.2010. The defendants No. 1-5 published a notice in the daily Kaler Kantha on 02.11.2010 stating the fact that the power of attorney dated 04.08.1999 has been cancelled on 29.07.2010. The plaintiffs filed a rejoinder of the paper publication dated 21.11.2010 and thereafter filed the above numbered suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The defendants No. 1-5 entered appearance and contested the suit by filing a written statement dated 25.07.2007 denying the material averments made in the plaint stating, <em>inter alia</em>, that since the plaintiff No. 2 failed to take any steps on the basis of power of attorney, they cancelled the same on 29.07.2010. Their further case was that they had not taken any money from the plaintiff No.2 Roksona Ameer and RAJUK did not accept the power of attorney, as such, the power has not been acted upon. The defendants No. 1-5 got sale permission from RAJUK and transferred the suit property on 21.04.2013 in favour of one Sakura Saber at a consideration of Taka 40,00,00,000/-and prayed for dismissal of the suit. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The plaintiff examined as many as 4 (four) witnesses, namely, P.W. 1 Zia Uddin, P.W. 2  Abdur Rahim, P.W. 3 Yunus Howladar and P.W. 4 Kabir Ahmed and they were also cross-examined by the defendants side  while the defendants No. 1-5 produced as many as 2 (two) witnesses  and they were also cross-examined by the plaintiffs. The trial Court after hearing the parties dismissed the suit by the impugned judgment and decree dated 20.11.2014 mainly on the ground that the plaintiff did not pray for any consequential relief for cancellation of the deed of cancellation of power of attorney. Another reason for dismissal of the suit was that the plaintiff could not proof the alleged transaction made between the parties. Being aggrieved by the impugned judgment and decree dated 20.11.2014 the plaintiff has preferred this appeal. During pendency of the appeal, the plaintiff filed an application for amendment of the plaint inserting a prayer for consequential relief of the cancellation of the deed of power of attorney and the same was allowed by the judgment and order of this Court dated 17.09.2015. Against the order of amendment of plaint, the defendant No. 1 went to the Appellate Division and initially leave was granted in Civil Appeal No. 201 of 2016. However the aforesaid Civil Appeal was dismissed by the Appellate Division subsequently and therefore, maintained the order of the High Court Division amending the plaint. Accordingly, the plaintiff-appellants deposited advalorum court fees.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 109%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%;">Mr. Abdul Wadud Bhuiyan, learned Advocate appearing for the appellants, at the very outset, submits that both the registered agreement for  sale and the power of attorney executed on the same day on 04.08.1999 and the power of attorney were drafted by the learned Advocate Md. Yunus Howladar  (P.W.1) who identified the executants of the bainapatra and the  same were executed in presence of some other witnesses,  namely, Abdul Hye and one Mahmud Hossain both are brothers-in-law of Md. Atiqur Rahman, the defendant No. 1 and as such the allegation as raised by the defendants  with regard to execution of power of attorney by undue influence is not correct at all inasmuch as the defendants failed to prove such undue influence. Having referred to the Clause 21 of the power of attorney Mr. Bhuiyan the learned Advocate submits further that the power of attorney was being with consideration, it was <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">irrevocable and it cannot be revoked unilaterally</span> in defying the provision of section 202 of the Contract Act, 1872. Mr. Bhuiyan submits further that the deed of agreement and the power of attorney should be read together and on the plain reading of the bainapatra it is apparent that the defendants took certain amount from the plaintiff No. 1 and the plaintiff No. 2 executed last bainapatra in favour of the plaintiff No.1 by virtue of the said power of attorney dated 04.08.1999. Mr. Bhuiyan, learned Advocate next submits that since the power of attorney is coupled with interest and as such it is not revocable. Mr. Bhuiyan further submits that the plaintiff No.2  spent huge amount of money in conducting the case, so it cannot be said that she failed to take any steps by virtue of power of attorney and as such the power of attorney has been acted upon and thus it cannot be cancelled unilaterally. Mr. Bhuiyan next submits that the defendants No.1-5 in violation of injunction order transferred the property in favour of one Sakura Saber on 21.04.2013 who mutated his name on 22.04.2013 in the office of RAJUK and as such the subsequent transfer by the principal is void and inoperative. Mr. Bhuiyan next submits that no notice has been served before cancellation of the power of attorney and as such cancellation of the same was illegal.  He next submits that the P.W. 1 Zia Uddin is the attesting witnesses of both the deeds of bainapatra as well as the power of attorney and as such he has got direct knowledge about the transaction and was competent to depose in the Court. The learned Advocate seeks to rely on the two decisions reported in 67 DLR (AD) (2015) 240 and AIR 1969 (Supreme Court) 73.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 107%;">Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, learned Advocate appearing for the respondents submits that on 04.08.1999 on the date of execution of bainapatra a power of attorney was executed in favour of the plaintiff No.2 by the defendants but no consideration money was passed against the power of attorney and the said power of attorney was not acted upon since no permission was accorded from the RAJUK to do the activities on the strength of the power. The learned Advocate submits further that according to clause 22 and 24 of the lease deed dated 13.03.1961 acceptance of power of attorney by the RAJUK is a must and the power of attorney holder must apply to the Deputy Director of RAJUK along with attested copy thereof and three attested signature of the power of attorney holder and one passport size photograph of the power of attorney holder and the principal but in the instant case the plaintiff No.2  never went to the RAJUK with the power of  attorney before 19.10.2010 and as such the power of attorney was not acted upon. Mr. Md. Nurul Amin next submits that an order of injunction was granted on 06.08.2012 not to transfer the property to anybody else by the trial Court and that injunction order was stayed on 08.10.2012 by the High Court Division in First Miscellaneous Appeal No. 8 of 2012 and thereafter the defendants No. 1-5 got sale permission on 24.03.2013 from RAJUK in order to transfer the property and the defendants executed and registered sale deed in favour of one Sakura Saber on 21.04.2013 when no restraining order was available upon the RAJUK. Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, learned Advocate next submits that the evidence of the P.W. 1 Zia Uddin is not an admissible evidence since he has no personal knowledge about the transaction allegedly made between the plaintiff No. 2 and the defendants. In support of his submission the learned Advocate has referred to a decision of Indian Supreme Court in the case of Man Kaur (Dead) by IRS Vs.-Hartar Singh Sangha passed in Civil Appeal Nos. 147-148 of 2001. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, learned Advocate next submits that when the plaintiff No.2 acted against the interest of the defendants No.1-5 they had cancelled the power of attorney on 29.07.2010 and the defendants served a legal notice through registered post upon the plaintiff no.2 informing her about the fact of such revocation of power of attorney. The learned Advocate next submits that before 19.10.2010 the plaintiff no.2 never went to the RAJUK for according permission or for acceptance of the power of attorney and hence the same was not acted upon. Mr. Md. Nurul Amin, learned Advocate next submits that it is the settle principle of law that in order to get the decree the plaintiff must prove his case.  Mere a statement in the plaint is no evidence in the eye of law unless it is proved by examining a competent witness on oath. Basing on the testimony of an attesting witness who has no personal knowledge about the alleged facts of transaction, the suit cannot be decreed. To substantiate his submission the learned Advocate referred to reliance on the case reported in 16 BLD (1996) 519 and 6 BLT (AD) (1998)1.  He finally submits that the trial Court on consideration of the material evidence on record rightly dismissed the suit and the appellant could not find out any infirmity with the judgment of the trial Court and as such the appeal is liable to be dismissed.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have heard the submissions of the learned Advocates for both the parties and perused the impugned judgment of the trial Court and have gone through the materials on record including the exhibits and the evidences of the parties. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It appears that the appellant preferred the aforesaid suit with a prayer that the power of attorney dated 04.08.1999 is still in force and the deed of cancellation of power of attorney dated 29.07.2012 is illegal, void and without jurisdiction. The trial Court framed as many as 4(four) issues to determine the suit. The parties adduced witnesses as P.Ws and D.Ws. in order to prove their respective cases and after hearing of the parties the suit was dismissed. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 109%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 109%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">The question arises before this Court whether the judgment and decree passed by the trial Court is liable to be interfered with or not. Since the suit is involved with regard to the question of revocation of power of attorney admittedly executed by the defendants No. 1-5 in favour of the plaintiff No. 2, we consider it prudent not to involve us or make any comment about the other proceedings pending in connection with the property in question in different courts including the Appellate Division which might affect the merit of those litigations inasmuch as the cancellation of power of attorney has no nexus with the agreement for sale that has been executed before cancellation of the power of attorney. Moreover, we are not dealing here with the validity of the agreement for sale and no issue regarding it had been framed by the trial Court. The defendants No. 1-5 executed and registered a power of attorney in favour of the plaintiff No.2 Roksona Ameer on 04.08.1999 in order to look after the suit property including the permission to sale of the same. At a later stage on 29.07.2009, the power of attorney had been revoked by another registered instrument. We have examined the power of attorney dated 04.08.1999 wherefrom it transpires that the attorney was given authority to negotiate the terms for sale, to settle the price, enter into the agreement for sale and sale the schedule properties with or without building etc. Clause 21 of the power of attorney contains that- “This power of attorney being for a consideration is irrevocable and shall be binding on us and our successors and heirs.” Neither mode of consideration, nor extent of consideration was recorded in the power of attorney, nor it is found that the power of attorney is coupled with interest except the aforesaid wordings. If the holder of power of attorney has not invested any money by herself/himself or paid any sum to the principal the power of attorney may be cancelled at any time assigning reasons of such cancellation. In the instant case from the deed of revocation of power of attorney, it appears that the principal revoked it assigning the reasons amongst others to the effect that- “as the purpose for which the attorney was appointed has been exhausted and in the context of the present unavailable circumstances, we have decided to handle the mater directly and by ourselves.” Except the power of attorney executed couple with interest all other power may be revoked at any time by the principal.  From the recital of the power of attorney, it does not appear that the agent herself has an interest in the property and hence such agency can be revoked unilaterally without prejudice of such interest. The question of agreement for sale made between the appellant No. 1 Khan Md. Ameer and the respondents No. 1-5 is altogether a different transaction of which the litigation is pending before the Appellate Division. Let us address the question whether before cancellation of the power of attorney a notice to that effect is a must or not. It appears that the provision for giving notice before cancellation of power of attorney has been incorporated in the new enactment of the Powers of Attorney Act, 2012 which was not expressly provided in repealed Act, 1982 thereof. It is not imperative to settle that the notice was served or not before cancellation of the power as we are of the opinion that the power of attorney in question is not a power coupled with interest and hence the same is revocable. Furthermore, since the power of attorney was revoked on 27.09.2009 before coming into force of new enactment, 2012, as such, we are of the view that  giving notice or no notice  has not debarred the principal to revoke it as the same appears do not have coupled with interest of the agent. The submissions of the learned Advocates for the respondents that lessee shall not sell, charge, mortgage, exchange the suit property without prior permission from RAJUK, the lessor, is also a different question. As part of due diligence exercise we looked into the provisions of RAJUK with regard to the acceptance of the power of attorney by it. Wherefrom it transpires that for the purpose of transfer of a lease-hold property, there is a provision to accrue permission from RAJUK and the matter of transfer of the property, if not registered in the office of lessor, the lessor will not be bound to recognize or accept any person as lessee of the property in place of the transferor. Since the permission from RAJUK is a pre-requisite, as such, devoid of such permission renders the power-of-attorney as ineffectual and unenforceable. The fiduciary relationship between the buyer and the attorney, husband and wife, is nothing but a sham since the attorney never acted in favour of her principal rather she has always been acting for her husband, the other party. We could not understand why the appellant kept silent long about 10 years to take permission from RAJUK for acceptance of the power of attorney or for accordance of permission to sale the property. From the materials on record, we do not find that the holder of power of attorney has ever approached to the RAJUK in order to accept the same in the office of RAJUK before 19.10.2010. It also appears that when RAJUK did not accept the power of attorney at last the holder of the power of attorney i.e. the plaintiff No. 2 moved this Court invoking writ jurisdiction and the Rule was issued and the same is still pending. The transaction between the plaintiff No. 1 and the defendants whatever <span style="letter-spacing: -0.5pt;">may be made with regard to execution of agreement</span> for sale is altogether a matter for another proceeding, namely, suit for specific performance of contract wherein the plaintiff got a decree from this Court and the respondents went to the Appellate Division and the same is  also still pending. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">With regard to the admissibility of the evidence of P.W. 1 Zia Uddin, we are of the view that this P.W. 1 has no personal knowledge with regard to the transaction allegedly made between the plaintiff No. 2 and the defendants No. 1-5 to show that the power of attorney is coupled with interest. However since the facts surrounding transaction between the plaintiff No.1 and the defendants No.1-5 is pending in another forum we refrain from making elaborate discussions on this issue. The defendants side denied about the fact of execution of agreement for sale with  the plaintiff No. 1 and  that they did not receive any part of consideration money from him would also be decided in the suit  for specific performance of contract whether the agreement for sale was a valid contract or not. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Considering the facts and circumstances of the case, we do not find any merit in the appeal. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly, the appeal is dismissed however there will be no order as to costs. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         Communicate a copy of this judgment at once.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" title=""><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 110%;">First Appeal No. 81 of 2015</span></strong></a></span></p></div></div></div></div>
535	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Khandaker Golam Mostafa and another Vs. Md. Sadequzzaman and others 2017 (2) LNJ (AD) 61</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 2208  OF  2014 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Muhammad Imman Ali. J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Shahidul Alam, Mr. Sharif Uddin Chaklader,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2017 (2) LNJ (AD) 61</p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Khandaker Golam Mostafa and another </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Sadequzzaman and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Civil Law</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2017-09-13</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if gte mso 9]><xml> <w:WordDocument>  <w:View>Normal</w:View> text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">2.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts relevant for disposal of the instant civil petition for leave to appeal are that the writ petitioner was appointed on 11.04.1998 as Headmaster of the Polytechnic Bilateral High School, Zummapara, Sadar, Rangpur (the School). By order dated 08.11.2007 the Managing Committee of the school suspended the writ petitioner temporarily from service and asked him to show cause as to why action should not be taken against him in respect of certain allegations as mentioned in the said notice. The writ petitioner replied on 27.03.2008 denying the allegations brought against him. Later on the writ petitioner was not allowed to attend the school and on several occasions the writ petitioner requested the managing committee for allowing him to sign on the attendance register and also to pay him subsistence allowance against the said order of temporary suspension, but to no effect. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">3.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Challenging the order of temporary suspension the writ petitioner instituted Other Class Suit Nos. 777 of 2007 before the Court of Assistant Judge, Taragonj, Rangpur and simultaneously the writ petitioner also filed writ petition No. 10798 of 2007 before the High Court Division. Eventually the suit was dismissed by the judgement and decree dated 21.03.2012 and the Rule issued in the writ petition was also discharged by the judgement and order dated 11.11.2008 and that both the proceedings failed on point of maintainability, the actions being found premature. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">4.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter, the writ petitioner received the impugned memo bearing No.2/Hp/ 1256/183/(10) dated 21.01.2013 issued by the Secondary and Higher Secondary Education Board, Dinajpur (the Board) approving dismissal order passed in respect of service of the writ petitioner. Challenging the said memo the respondent herein as petitioner filed Writ Petition No. 3565 of 2013 before the High Court Division and obtained Rule.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">5.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The Headmaster (in charge) of the school as writ respondent No. 13 filed an affidavit-in-opposition controverting the statements as made in the writ petition. He contended, <em>inter alia,</em> that bringing certain allegations as to <span style="letter-spacing: -0.4pt;">misappropriation of fund and other irregularities</span> the managing committee of the school by their resolution decided to suspend the petitioner <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">temporarily to initiate a departmental proceeding.</span> Accordingly, by the letter dated 08.11.2007 the </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">writ</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> petitioner was suspended temporarily from service and was also asked to show cause against the allegations as mentioned in the show cause notice and the writ petitioner replied against the show cause notice. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">6.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Thereafter, a three member enquiry committee was constituted pursuant to “the Recognized Non-Government Secondary School Teachers (Board of Intermediate and Secondary Education, Rajshahi) Terms and Conditions of Service Regulations, 1979” (the Regulations, 1979). The enquiry committee submitted report on 12.12.2007 recommending to dismiss the petitioner from service as the allegations brought against him were found true and genuine. On the basis of the said enquiry report, the managing committee of the school by their resolution dated 13.12.2007 dismissed the petitioner from service pursuant to regulation 12 of the Regulations, 1979. Thereafter, the Appeal and Arbitration Committee of the Board by their resolution dated 05.01.2013 recommended to approve the order of dismissal. Accordingly, the Board in its meeting dated 08.01.2013 approved the order of dismissal pursuant to the regulation 12 of the Regulations, 1979 and it was communicated to the writ petitioner by the memo dated 21.01.2013. In view of the facts, the writ petitioner was dismissed from service following the procedures as laid down in the Regulations, 1979. Further contentions of this </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">writ</span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> respondent are that the writ petitioner unsuccessfully filed Title Suit Nos. 777 of 2007 and the writ petition No. 10768 of 2007 challenging the action dismissing his service.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">7.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In due course after hearing both the parties by the impugned judgement and order the said Rule was made absolute. Hence, the writ respondent Nos. 6 and 13 as petitioners have filed the instant civil petition for leave to appeal before this Division. </span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">8.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Shahidul Islam, learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioners submitted that the impugned Memo dated 21.01.2013 was legally issued by the proper authority approving the dismissal of the writ petitioner in accordance with the recommendation of the Appeal and Arbitration Board dated 05.01.2013. He further submitted that the High Court Division erred in basing its decision upon consideration that the dismissal of the writ petitioner was based on surmise and conjecture since against the order of suspension dated 08.11.2007 the writ petitioner filed Other Suit No. 777 of 2007 against the Managing Committee of the School and that suit was dismissed. He also submitted that the High Court Division misconstrued and misunderstood the materials on record in considering that the Rule issued in Writ Petition No. 10768 of 2007 had been discharged as premature and that was the reason behind the decision to approve his dismissal. He submitted that the High Court Division failed to appreciate the facts and circumstances of the case in their true perspective and did not consider the fact that, prior to his dismissal, notice was served upon the writ petitioner to show cause on 18.12.2012 with regard to the allegations brought against him and he also appeared before the Appeal and Arbitration Committee in its 5<sup>th</sup> meeting on 05.01.2013, and after hearing the writ petitioner the committee recommended to approve the final dismissal from service of the writ petitioner and on the strength of that resolution the President, Board Committee and Chairman of the Secondary and Higher Secondary Education Board, Denajpur on <span style="letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">08.01.2013 unanimously  approved the decisions</span> of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee. He submitted that the High Court Division misdirected itself in considering that the dismissal of the writ petitioner was based on the findings of the Courts in the suit as well as the earlier writ petition. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">            </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Sharif Uddin Chaklader, learned Advocate</span><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;"> appearing for respondent No. 1 made submissions in support of the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocates for the parties concerned, perused the impugned judgement and order as well as the evidence and materials on record. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">11.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">It is a fact that challenging the temporary suspension of the writ petitioner Other Class Suit No. 777 of 2007 was instituted by him before the Court of the Assistant Judge, Taragonj, Rangpur and at the same time he filed Writ Petition No. 10768 of 2007 before the High Court Division. Both the actions by the writ petitioner-respondent No. 1 herein resulted in failure due to the fact that his actions were premature. Subsequently, an Inquiry Committee submitted its report on 12.12.2007 which recommended the writ petitioner’s dismissal from service and on the basis of the said report the Managing Committee by resolution dated 13.12.2007 dismissed the petitioner from service. That dismissal was seemingly approved by the Appeal and Arbitration Committee by resolution dated 05.01.2013 and the Education Board approved the order of dismissal in its meeting dated 08.01.2013, which was communicated to the writ petitioner by the impugned Memo dated 21.01.2013. But a close scrutiny of the resolution of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee is required.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">12.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">We find from the impugned judgement that the High Court Division noted that the Appeal and Arbitration Committee in their meeting dated 05.01.2013 took the following resolution:</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">“</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">B­m¡QÉ ¢houx 2</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">f¢m­VL¢eL EµQ ¢hcÉ¡mu, pcl, lwf¤l Hl fËd¡e ¢nrL Se¡h ®j¡x p¡­cL¥‹¡j¡e Hl Q§s¡¿¹ hlM¡­Ù¹l ¢ho­u B­m¡Qe¡ J ¢pÜ¡¿¹ NËqZz </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">¢pÜ¡¿¹x lwf¤l ®Sm¡l pcl Ef­Sm¡d£e f¢m­VL¢eL EµQ ¢hcÉ¡mu Hl fËd¡e ¢nrL Se¡h ®j¡x p¡­cL¥‹¡j¡e Hl Q¨s¡¿¹ hlM¡­Ù¹l ¢ho­u ¢hÙ¹¡¢la B­m¡Qe¡ quz A¢ik¤š² fËd¡e ¢nrL LaÑªL c¡­ulLªa j¡jm¡l l¡u fË¢aù¡­el f­r<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>qJu¡u a¡­L Q¡L¥l£ q­a hlM¡­Ù¹l ¢hou¢V Ae¤­j¡ce Ll¡l SeÉ p¤f¡¢ln Ll¡ qmz</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">”</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">       </span></span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">The High Court Division observed that the two proceedings, namely the suit filed before the Assistant Judge and the earlier writ petition, were initiated challenging the order of temporary suspension and the writ petitioner lost the same on the ground that the proceedings were initiated against a premature action. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">14.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong></span><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">The resolution of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee clearly shows that the writ petitioner’s dismissal was approved because the decision of the Courts were in favour of the authority</span> “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">A¢ik¤š² fËd¡e ¢nrL LaÑªL c¡­ulLªa j¡jm¡l l¡u fË¢aù¡­el f­r<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>qJu¡u a¡­L Q¡L¥l£ q­a hlM¡­Ù¹l ¢hou¢V Ae¤­j¡ce Ll¡l SeÉ p¤f¡¢ln Ll¡ qmz</span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;">” <span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">Hence, it is clear that the approval given by the Committee was influenced by the fact that the cases filed by the writ petitioner were decided against him.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-AU;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      <span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">  </span></span></span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">We also find from the impugned judgement that the High Court Division considered that the inquiry report shows that the Inquiry Committee did not examine any witness to come to their decision, and therefore, the inquiry was not held in accordance with the requirement of Regulations, 1979. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">16.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The High Court Division concluded as follows: </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: times new roman,times,serif;">         “Therefore, it is apparent that in the aforesaid judgements of the civil suit and the writ petition were related to temporary suspension order and that the issue as to propriety of dismissal order through a departmental proceeding was not adjudicated in those proceedings. Despite the Appeal and Arbitration Committee justified the dismissal order referring to those judgements and as such we are of the view that the decision of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee was not based on record and proper exercise of their jurisdiction.”  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">17.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above, we are of the opinion that the impugned notice served by the Managing Committee was based on the approval of the Board, which was in turn based on the approval of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee, which was given on account of the decisions reached by the Courts in favour of the authority. As we noted earlier, the decisions of the Courts were against the Head Teacher because the challenge was against his temporary suspension order, and the decision were not on merit of the allegations brought against him.  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">18.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN-AU" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On scrutiny it is apparent that the approval of the Appeal and Arbitration Committee was not based on the consideration of the report of the Inquiry Committee. In any event, we find that the High Court Division has noted that the Inquiry Committee did not examine any witness to come to their decision and, therefore, the inquiry was not held in accordance with the requirement of Regulations, 1979. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">19.<span style="font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal; font-feature-settings: normal; font-language-override: normal; font-kerning: auto; font-synthesis: weight style; font-variant: normal;">        </span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">In the facts and circumstances detailed above, we do not find any illegality or infirmity in the impugned judgement and order of the High Court Division. In our view, the judgement does not call for any interference by this Division. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">         Accordingly, the civil petition for leave to appeal is dismissed.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 2208<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2014</span></u></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 10<sup>th</sup> of June, 2014 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 3564 of 2013)</span></p></div></div></div></div>

roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%;">}</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt;">}</span></strong></span></p></td><td style="width: 94.05pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;" width="125"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal;">M/S Project Builders Ltd. (PBL) of PBL Tower, (Level 5<sup>th</sup> and 6<sup>th</sup>), 17 North C/A, Gulshan-2, Dhaka-112; Represented by it Managing Director Mr. Aminul Islam.</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoHeading8" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-style: normal;">. . .Petitioner</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoHeading8" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-style: normal;">-Versus-</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-style: normal;">The Joint Venture of Messer’s China National Technical Import and Export Corporation and Messer’s Beijing Sound Environmental Engineering Company Limited, represented by its project manager Mr. Chen Hongye, CNTIC-BSEEC-JV of-Jiuling Building, No.-21, Xisanhusanbeilu, Haidian District, Beijing, Peoples Republic of China; at present of Karnaphuli Water Supply Project, KWSP-C-1, Pumra, Rangunia, Chittagong and others.</span></strong></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; font-style: normal;">...Opposite Party</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Sections 3 and 12</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">The parties to any agreement are free to insert a <em>forum selection clause</em> and/or a <em>choice of law clause</em> for resolution of contractual disputes. A <em>forum selection clause</em> in a contract with a conflict of laws element as in the present case allows parties to initiate litigation in a specific forum. Such clause may take the form of both requiring a specific process (for example, arbitration as in the present instance) to be carried out in a specific location.                                             . . .(13)</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 3</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">A distinction also has to be drawn between a <em>forum selection clause</em> and a <em>choice of law</em> c<em>lause.</em> Parties are usually free to nominate the proper law under which all relevant disputes are to be resolved. If there is an express selection, as in this case of Bangladeshi law, this choice will be respected by this Court so long it is made bona fide. It is under this head that the question of extent of application of the Act in the facts becomes moot. This Court finds Section 3(1) and (2) to exclude in that regard the operation of the Act in governing the arbitration procedure leaving the agreed terms of contract to accord primacy to the ICA of the ICC governed by the ICC Rules to set the forum and procedure for arbitration. This Court substantiates that finding by delving further into the genesis of the Act and its exact operational parameter relative to the requirements of the applicable international legal régime.                                              . . .(14)</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Arbitration Act (I of 2001)</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 3</span></strong></span></p><p> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-family: times new roman,times,serif;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">This Court is of the view that the conundrum resultantly posed by these widely divergent modes of interpretation and application of Section 3 makes it imperative for the scope and application of Section 3 to be revisited and thrashed out on the floor of the legislature rather than the halls of justice to clearly indicate its true intent and purport.
